These\n/// requirements are then verified and proved by the closure's\n/// creating function. This struct encodes those requirements.\n///\n/// The requirements are listed as being between various `RegionVid`. The 0th\n/// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\n/// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\n/// appearance. When an\n/// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n/// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n/// outlives relationship.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug)]\npub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n    /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n    /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n    Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n\n    /// Subject is a free region from the closure. Indicates a requirement\n    /// like `'a: 'b` being passed to the caller; the region here is `'a`.\n    Region(ty::RegionVid),\n}\n\n/// Represents a `ty::Ty` for use in [`ClosureOutlivesSubject`].\n///\n/// This abstraction is necessary because the type may include `ReVar` regions,\n/// which is what we use internally within NLL code, and they can't be used in\n/// a query response.\n#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\npub struct ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n    inner: Ty<'tcx>,\n}\n// DO NOT implement `TypeVisitable` or `TypeFoldable` traits, because this\n// TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Self {\n        let inner = fold_regions(tcx, ty, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n            ty::ReVar(vid) => {\n                let br = ty::BoundRegion {\n                    var: ty::BoundVar::from_usize(vid.index()),\n                    kind: ty::BoundRegionKind::Anon,\n                };\n                ty::Region::new_bound(tcx, depth, br)\n            }\n            _ => bug!(\"unexpected region in ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy: {r:?}\"),\n        });\n\n        Self { inner }\n    }\n\n    pub fn instantiate(\n        self,\n        tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n        mut map: impl FnMut(ty::RegionVid) -> ty::Region<'tcx>,\n    ) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n        fold_regions(tcx, self.inner, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n            ty::ReBound(ty::BoundVarIndexKind::Bound(debruijn), br) => {\n                debug_assert_eq!(debruijn, depth);\n                map(ty::RegionVid::from_usize(br.var.index()))\n            }\n            _ => bug!(\"unexpected region {r:?}\"),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\nstruct CollectRegionConstraintsResult<'tcx> {\n    infcx: BorrowckInferCtxt<'tcx>,\n    body_owned: Body<'tcx>,\n    promoted: 262→                // successor locations.\n   263→                debug!(\"borrow {:?} gets killed at {:?}\", borrow_index, kill_location);\n   264→ visit_stack: vec![],\n            body,\n            regioncx,\n            borrows_out_of_scope_at_location: FxIndexMap::default(),\n        };\n        for (borrow_index, borrow_data) in borrow_set.iter_enumerated() {\n            let borrow_region = borrow_data.region;\n            let location = borrow_data.reserve_location;\n            prec.precompute_borrows_out_of_scope(borrow_index, borrow_region, location);\n        }\n\n        prec.borrows_out_of_scope_at_location\n    }\n\n    fn precompute_borrows_out_of_scope(\n        &mut self,\n        borrow_index: BorrowIndex,\n        borrow_region: RegionVid,\n        first_location: Location,\n    ) {\n        let first_block = first_location.block;\n        let first_bb_data = &self.body.basic_blocks[first_block];\n\n        // This is the first block, we only want to visit it from the creation of the borrow at\n        // `first_location`.\n        let first_lo =          first_block,\n            first_lo,\n            first_hi,\n        ) {\n            let kill_location = Location { block: first_block, statement_index: kill_stmt };\n            // If region     self.borrows_out_of_scope_at_location\n                .entry(kill_location)\n                .or_default()\n                .push(borrow_index);\n\n            // The borrow is already dead, there is no need to visit other blocks.\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // The borrow is not dead. Add successor BBs to the work list, if necessary.\n        for succ_bb in first_bb_data.terminator().successors() {\n            if self.visited.insert(succ_bb) {\n                self.visit_stack.push(succ_bb);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // We may end up visiting `first_block` again. This is not an issue: we know at this point\n        // that it does not kill the borrow in the `first_lo..=first_hi` range, so checking the\n        // `0..first_lo` range and the `0..first_hi` range give the same result.\n        while let Some(block) = self.visit_stack.pop() {\n            let bb_data = &self.body[block];\n            let num_stmts = bb_data.statements.len();\n            if let Some(kill_stmt) =\n                self.regioncx.first_non_contained_inclusive(borrow_region, block, 0, num_stmts)\n            {\n                let kill_location = Location { block, statement_index: kill_stmt };\n                // If region does not contain a point at the location, then add to list and skip\n                // successor locations.\n .or_default()\n                    .push(borrow_index);\n\n                // We killed the borrow, so we do not visit this block's successors.\n                continue;\n            }\n\n            // Add successor BBs to the work list, if necessary.\n            for succ_bb in bb_data.terminator().successors() {\n                if self.visited.insert(succ_bb) {\n                    self.visit_stack.push(succ_bb);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        self.visited.clear();\n    }\n}\n\n// This is `pub` because it's used by unstable external borrowck data users, Otherwise, we'll pass in `None` to the\n        // functions below, which will trigger them to report errors\n        // eagerly.\n        let mut outlives_requirements = infcx.tcx.is_typeck_child(mir_def_id).then(Vec::new);\n\n        self.check_type_tests(infcx, outlives_requirements.as_mut(), &mut errors_buffer);\n\n        debug!(?errors_buffer);\n        debug!(?outlives_requirements);\n\n        // In Polonius mode, the errors about missing universal region relations are in the output\n        // and need to be emitted or propagated. Otherwise, we need to check whether the\n        // constraints were too strong, and if so, emit or propagate those errors.\n        if infcx.tcx.sess.opts.unstable_opts.polonius.is_legacy_enabled() {\n            self.check_polonius_subset_errors(\n                outlives_requirements.as_mut(),\n                &mut errors_buffer,\n                polonius_output\n                    .as_ref()\n                    .expect(\"Polonius output is unavailable despite `-Z polonius`\"),\n            );\n        } else {\n            self.check_universal_regions(outlives_requirements.as_mut(), &mut errors_buffer);\n        }\n\n        debug!(?errors_buffer);\n\n        let outlives_requirements = outlives_requirements.unwrap_or_default();\n\n        if outlives_requirements.is_empty() {\n            (None, errors_buffer)\n        } else {\n            let num_external_vids = self.universal_regions().num_global_and_external_regions();\n            (\n                Some(ClosureRegionRequirements { num_external_vids, outlives_requirements }),\n                errors_buffer,\n            )\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Propagate the region constraints: this will grow the values\n    /// for each region variable until all the constraints are\n    /// satisfied. Note that some values may grow **too** large to be\n    /// feasible, but we check this later.\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    fn propagate_constraints(&mut self) {\n        debug!(\"constraints={:#?}\", {\n            let mut constraints: Vec<_> = self.outlives_constraints().collect();\n            constraints.sort_by_key(|c| (c.sup, c.sub));\n            constraints\n                .into_iter()\n                .map(|c| (c, self.constraint_sccs.scc(c.sup), self.constraint_sccs.scc(c.sub)))\n                .collect::<Vec<_>>()\n        });\n\n        // To propagate constraints, we walk the DAG induced by the\n        // SCC.
